1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Agentic Correctness: Implement Minimal GCC GIMPLE Pass

## Your Task

Write C/C++ source files implementing a minimal GCC GIMPLE optimization pass that counts basic blocks per function. Your implementation must follow GCC's established patterns: 1. Define a `pass_data` struct and inherit from `gimple_opt_pass` as seen in existing passes. 2. Implement `gate()` and `execute()` virtual methods following the pattern in `gcc/tree-ssa-dce.cc`. 3. Register the pass using `make_pass_*()` factory function as defined in `gcc/tree-pass.h`. 4. Use `dump_file` for debug output following existing patterns. Write your files to `/workspace/`. Also write `/workspace/answer.json` listing the GCC source files you referenced.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?
- **Keyword presence**: Are required terms present in your explanation?

pass implementation follows the established patterns found in the GCC codebase, particularly drawing from tree-ssa-dce.cc and gimple-laddress.cc as primary references. The implementation demonstrates the four key components of a GCC GIMPLE pass: (1) the pass_data struct that holds metadata about the pass including type (GIMPLE_PASS), name, optimization group flags, and properties; (2) a class that inherits from gimple_opt_pass (defined in gcc/tree-pass.h) which is itself derived from opt_pass; (3) virtual method implementations for gate() which determines if the pass should run and execute() which contains the pass logic; and (4) a factory function (make_pass_bb_count) that creates and returns a new instance of the pass. The execute method iterates over all basic blocks in a function using the FOR_EACH_BB_FN macro from gcc/basic-block.h, counting them and reporting the result to the dump_file for debugging output. This pattern is consistent across all GCC GIMPLE passes including the Dead Code Elimination pass (pass_dce) in gcc/tree-ssa-dce.cc and the Lower Address pass (pass_laddress) in gcc/gimple-laddress.cc. The pass integrates into GCC's optimization pipeline by being registered in gcc/passes.def and can be invoked during compilation with appropriate -fdump-tree flags.\"\n}\n",

1. WRITE /workspace/tree-bb-count.cc
/* Basic block counting pass for the GNU compiler.
   Copyright (C) 2026 Free Software Foundation, Inc.

This file is part of GCC.

GCC is free software; you can redistribute it and/or modify it
under the terms of the GNU General Public License as published by the
Free Software Foundation; either version 3, or (at your option) any
later version.

GCC is distributed in the hope that it will be useful, but WITHOUT
ANY WARRANTY; without even the implied warranty of MERCHANTABILITY or
FITNESS FOR A PARTICULAR PURPOSE.  See the GNU General Public License
for more details.

You should have received a copy of the GNU General Public License
along with GCC; see the file COPYING3.  If not see
<http://www.gnu.org/licenses/>.  */

/* Basic block counter.

   This is a simple GIMPLE optimization pass that counts the number of
   basic blocks in each function and outputs the result to the dump file.

   This pass demonstrates the standard GCC pattern for writing a
   GIMPLE optimization pass:
   1. Define a pass_data struct with metadata
   2. Inherit from gimple_opt_pass
   3. Implement gate() and execute() virtual methods
   4. Register the pass using a make_pass_*() factory function
*/

#include "config.h"
#include "system.h"
#include "coretypes.h"
#include "backend.h"
#include "tree.h"
#include "gimple.h"
#include "tree-pass.h"
#include "basic-block.h"
#include "dumpfile.h"
